وقتاً لأداء واجب آخر، فبنذره لا يخرج صوم اليوم عن قبول وصف الوجوب، وإلا لزم المشروع، وهو معصية، ولا نذر بها، وأما إبطال النفلية فكان فيه مأذوناً من الشارع، فوقت النذر المعين محل لإيقاع الصوم مع وصف الكفارة مثلاً، وإن كان إيقاعه، إثماً لتفويت واجب النذر فانكشف الفرق بأتم وجه فلا تصغ إلى من يقول : لا فرق بين النذر ورمضان، لأنهما فرضان فلم يبق في الوقت مباينهما مشروعاً، فينبغي أن يتحد حكمهما (والحج ذو شبهين) شبه (بالمعيار، و) شبه بـ (الظرف، فإنه لا يسع في عام واحد إلا واحداً) وبهذا شابه المعيار، كما إلا واجباً واحداً ولا يستغرق فعله وقته الذي هو أشهر الحج، وهذا آية الاتساع، وفيه يسع أن العام الواحد بعض من الوقت فإن وقته العمر كله فلا يصلح شبهاً بالمعيارية، وإلا فوقت الصلاة أيضاً معيار، إذ بعضه لا إلا صلاة واحدة، ثم عدم استغراق فعله تمام الوقت لا يسع لا يكفي للظرفية، بل سعة الوقت بفعل آخر مثله وليس أشهر العام الواحد كذلك، وها هنا وجه آخر للإشكال، أي لكونه ذا شبهين هو أن العام الأول لا يصلح إلا حجاً واحداً والتأخير عنه إثم فهو وقته والعام الآخر مشكوك فتعين للأداء فبهذا الوجه معيار وإن وجد أعوام أخرى فهي أيضاً صالحة لأداء الحج، فوسع الوقت الذي هو العمر حجاً آخر، وبهذا الوجه صار ظرفاً، كذا ذكره القاضي الإمام أبو زيد في الأسرار»، ولعل هذا الوجه هو مراد الإمام فخر الإسلام بقوله : ومعنى قولنا إنه مشكل أن وقته العمر ، وأشهر الحج في كل عام صالحة لأدائه أم أشهر الحج من العام الأول وقت متعين لأدائه؟ ويمكن حمل عبارة المتن عليه أيضاً، ثم هذا الوجه إنما يتم على رأي الإمام أبي يوسف رحمه الله فإنه يرى التعجيل واجباً، وأما على رأي الإمام محمد رحمه الله فنسبة العمر إليه نسبة وقت الظهر إليه فإن قلت الحج وإن كان وقته العمر لكنه يحتمل الموت قبل إدراك العام الثاني فالعام الأول يحتمل أن يكون هو العمر فيتضيق الوقت، ويحتمل أن يكون بعض العمر فيتسع قلت هذا لا يوجب وقوع التحديد من الشارع، بل مثله مثل الزكاة إذا تضيقت بقرب الموت والصلاة إذا تضيقت بالتأخير، بخلاف قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله فإن الوجوب عنده شرعاً على الفور، لاحتمال الموت، فيتضيق شرعاً، فإذا عاش ولم يحج العام الأول تضيق الثاني شرعاً، وصار هو مع العام الأول موسعاً، فافهم وتأمل فإنه حقيق به ومن ها هنا أي من أجل شبهة بالمعيار والظرف أعطى حكماً بين حكميهما فقلنا : يتأدى فرضه بمطلق النية، ويقع عن النفل إذا نواه) وإنما لم يعكس، لأن النفلية تضاد الفرضية وليست مبطلة له كما في المعيار، والإطلاق لا يضادها، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أنه : هل يصلح العام الأول النفل أم لا؟ وعلى الثاني يلزم أن يصح بنية النفل أيضاً، وعلى الأول فلا يكفي الإطلاق، فإن المؤدى لم يتعين للفرض وأيضاً الواجب، وإن كان واجباً فورياً، لكن غايته حرمة غيره لا أنه صار الوقت في حق ما عداه كالمحرم، فلا بد من نية التعين بخلاف شهر رمضان والحق في وجهه أن في الحج توسعة حتى حكم رسول الله لتلك كل المرأة إن حج ابنك وكان غير عاقل تام فاكتفى بنية أمه، فأولى أن بنية مطلقة من الحاج وأما النفلية فمضادة بالكلية فلا يصح بنيتها هذا والله أعلم بمراد عباده وهو علام الغيوب.
The second article on rulings: If its absolute [meaning] were permissible, then its obligation would have no benefit; rather, fasting would be removed from consideration except a little, like nonexistent, so understand. (And the criterion may not be a cause for obligation, like a specific vow, which is performed with an absolute intention and with the intention of supererogatory [act] except in an unselected narration, because for the vower on that day there was one fast, and he could describe it with the description of supererogatory and other than it. When he vowed it, it became obligatory, so it cannot be described as supererogatory, and other than it is not valid until it is described as supererogatory. So this day in relation to supererogatory is like nights in relation to all fasting; thus the supererogatory is canceled and the intention of fasting on this day remains, and its realization is only the vowed [fast], so it is valid. It is not performed with the intention of another obligatory [fast] like make-up and expiation, without dispute in a narration, unlike Ramadan, which is valid with any intention, as a distinction between the obligation of Allah and the obligation of the servant. By the obligation of Allah, the fast of Ramadan becomes with the description of obligatory, so it cannot be described with another description, and other than it is not possible for it to be described. As for the vowed, it becomes specific by his vow, and the days of life were a time for performing another obligation. By his vow, the fast of the day is not removed from accepting the description of obligation; otherwise, the legislated would be necessary, and it is disobedience, and no vow includes it. As for canceling the supererogatory, he was permitted by the Lawgiver. So the time of the specific vow is a place for performing the fast with the description of expiation for example, even if performing it is a sin for missing the vowed obligation. Thus the difference is fully uncovered, so do not listen to those who say there is no difference between vow and Ramadan because both are obligatory, so no antipode remains in the time legislated, so their ruling should be unified. (And Hajj has two similarities: similarity to the criterion and similarity to the container, for it does not accommodate in one year except one) and by this it resembles the criterion, as it does not accommodate except one obligation, and its performance does not occupy its entire time, which is the months of Hajj, and this is a sign of breadth. And in it, one year accommodates part of the time, for its time is all of life, so it is not fit for similarity to criterion; otherwise, the time of prayer is also a criterion, for part of it does not accommodate except one prayer. Then the non-occupation of its performance of the entire time does not suffice for container-ness; rather, the breadth of time for another similar act, and the months of one year are not like that. And here is another aspect of the difficulty: that the first year does not accommodate except one Hajj, and delay from it is a sin, so it is its time, and the second year is doubtful, so it becomes specific for performance; by this aspect it is a criterion. Even if other years exist, they are also fit for performing Hajj, so the time which is life is broadened for another Hajj, and by this aspect it becomes a container. Thus mentioned by Judge Imam Abu Zayd in al-Asrar. Perhaps this aspect is intended by Imam Fakhr al-Islam in his statement: 'The meaning of our saying that it is difficult is: is its time life, and the months of Hajj in each year are fit for its performance, or are the months of Hajj from the first year a specific time for its performance?' And the expression of the text can also be carried upon it. Then this aspect is only valid according to the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, for he holds that haste is obligatory. As for the opinion of Imam Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, the relation of life to it is like the relation of the time of Zuhr to it. If you say: Hajj, though its time is life, yet death may occur before reaching the second year, so the first year may be the entire life, so time becomes restricted, and it may be part of life, so it becomes broad. I say: This does not necessitate specification from the Lawgiver; rather, it is like Zakat when it becomes restricted by nearness of death, and prayer when it becomes restricted by delay. Contrary to the saying of Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, for obligation in his view is immediate by law due to possibility of death, so it becomes restricted legally. If he lives and does not perform Hajj in the first year, the second becomes restricted legally, and it together with the first becomes broad. So understand and reflect, for it is worthy of it. And from here, i.e., because of its similarity to the criterion and the container, it was given a ruling between their two rulings. So we said: Its obligatory duty is performed with an absolute intention, and it counts as supererogatory if one intends it. And it was not reversed because supererogatoriness contradicts obligatory-ness but does not nullify it as in the criterion, and absoluteness does not contradict it. And it does not escape you whether the first year is fit for supererogatory or not? On the second, it necessitates that it is valid with the intention of supererogatory also, and on the first, the absolute intention is insufficient, for what is performed is not specified as obligatory. Also, the obligatory, though it is immediate, its utmost is prohibition of other than it, not that the time becomes like a sanctuary with respect to other than it, so the intention of specification is necessary, unlike the month of Ramadan. And the truth in its aspect is that in Hajj there is breadth, until the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, ruled for that woman: 'If your son performs Hajj...' and he was not fully rational, so he sufficed with his mother's intention, so an absolute intention from the pilgrim is more appropriate. As for supererogatoriness, it is completely contradictory, so it is not valid with its intention. This, and Allah knows best His servants' intent, and He is the Knower of the unseen.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the second article on rulings, specifically about the 'criterion' (المعيار) and its application to obligations. The author begins by explaining that if the absolute meaning of the criterion were permissive, it would render obligation useless. He then distinguishes between two types of obligations: those imposed by Allah (like Ramadan) and those imposed by the servant through a vow (nathr). For a vow, the act can be performed with an absolute intention and even with the intention of supererogatory acts in a non-preferred narration, because the day was originally available for any fast. Once vowed, it becomes obligatory, but the supererogatory intention is canceled. Unlike Ramadan, which is fixed as obligatory from the start, so it cannot be performed with another intention. The author emphasizes that there is a clear difference between divine obligation and human vow. 

Then the passage discusses Hajj, which has two aspects: it resembles the criterion (since it can only be performed once a year) and a container (since its time is one's entire life). The author examines the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding immediacy. Abu Yusuf holds that obligation is immediate due to possibility of death, so the first year is the specific time. Muhammad compares it to the time of Zuhr prayer, where the entire life is the time. The author reconciles that Hajj's ruling is between the two. Finally, he concludes that the obligatory Hajj is performed with an absolute intention and counts as supererogatory if intended, but not vice versa, because supererogatoriness contradicts the obligatory nature.

Key Terms
المعيار (al-mi'yar): The criterion: a time period that accommodates only one obligatory act and no other act of the same type.
النذر (al-nadhr): A vow: an obligation created by the servant's own pledge, making a specific act obligatory.
الظرف (al-zarf): Container: a time period that can accommodate more than one obligation, not entirely occupied by a single act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason a vowed fast differs from the Ramadan fast regarding intention?
A) The vowed fast cannot be performed with any intention because it is more severe.
B) Ramadan is divinely ordained from the start, so its time is a criterion; a vow transforms a container into a criterion, so only the vowed intention works.
C) Both are obligatory, so they have the same ruling on intention.
D) The vowed fast can be performed with the intention of nafl because it is a human obligation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi concept of al-mi'yar distinguishes between divine obligations that fix time as a criterion from the start and human vows that transform a container into a criterion, affecting the validity of different intentions.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Time for Performing an Expanded Obligation
Explaining the ruling on the time of an expanded obligation (واجب موسع)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the time of an expanded obligation, contrast it with the Shafi'i position, and apply the ruling to a practical scenario.

Core Idea
The entire time of an expanded obligation is valid for performance; constant resolve is not required.

This passage addresses a fundamental usul question: when a duty has a wide time window, what exactly is required at each moment? The Hanafi school holds that the entire time is designated for the act itself, while some Shafi'is argue that at every moment one owes either the act or a resolve to perform it. Understanding this difference clarifies how obligations bind the mukallaf and has practical implications for daily worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on expanded obligation
Read the opening statement: 'when the obligation is expanded, all of the time is a time for its performance, so the responsible person is free to choose to perform it at any time.' This is the Hanafi default.
The entire time window is valid; no part is singled out.
2
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Al-Baqillani and most Shafi'is hold that at every moment the obligation is either the act or the resolve (azm) as a substitute. They do not require renewal of resolve in every moment.
They argue that this prevents neglect of the obligation.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The passage refutes the Shafi'i argument that multiple substitutes are needed. It argues that a single continuous resolve (like the intention for prayer) suffices, and that the substituted (obligation) is one, not multiple.
The Hanafi use the example of expiation characteristics to show that one substitute can exist across multiple moments.
4
Examine the dialectical exchange
The text imagines an objection: 'the obligation is only one prayer, not many.' The Hanafi replies that the absolute resolve substitutes for the absolute prayer, and its extension covers the time.
This reinforces that a single continuous resolve is sufficient.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
For a person who intends to pray early but delays without renewing intention: Hanafi says no sin until the end; Shafi'i says sin if there is no resolve at later moments.
The footnote about Hajj expansion supports the concept of expansion.

مسألة وقت أداء الواجب الموسع (1) يصح إذا كان الواجب موسعاً فجميع الوقت وقت لأدائه فيتخير المكلف أن يأتي به في أي وقت شاء من وقته المقدر، ولا يترك في كل الوقت قال القاضي أبو بكر الباقلاني (وأكثر الشافعية الواجب في كل وقت الفعل أو العزم بدلاً، ويتعين الفعل (آخراً ولا يوجبون) أي هؤلاء (تجديد العزم في كل جزء) حتى إن أخل بالعزم في الجزء الثاني عصى (بل) يجوز أن يكون مذهبهم العزم الأول ينسحب انسحاب النية إلى أن يتضيق فلا يرد ما في «المنهاج» أن البدل متعدد والمبدل واحد وذلك لم يوجد في الشرع وجه عدم الورود أنا لا سلم تعدد البدل، فإنه لم ينص عليه فيجوز أن يكون واحداً منسحباً انسحاب النية، وأما إذا وجد العزمان فليس كل بدلاً بالذات، بل البدل أحدهما الموجود في ضمنهما، كما في خصال الكفارة»، إذ خصوص الأول، والثاني لا دخل له في «البدلية على أن المبدل أيضاً متعدد، فإن (إيقاعات الفعل بعدد الأجزاء أي عدد أجزاء الوقت ولا شك أن تلك الإيقاعات واجبة بدلاً، فإنه إن لم يؤد في أول الوقت فيجب الإيقاع الثاني، وهكذا فكذا أعزامها متعددة (فتساوي) الإيقاعات (الأعزام) الأبدال، فإن قيل : الواجب ليس إلا الصلاة ولا تعدد فيها، وإنما تعدد في الإيقاعات الجزئية، فالمبدل واحد والبدل كثير قلت : العزم المطلق عزم واحد بدل الصلاة المطلقة، وجزئياته كجزئياته، فإن قلت : الشرع إنما أوجب صلاة واحدة لا صلوات، لكن موسعاً، فيجب في كل جزء بدلاً صلاة واحدة والعزم البدل إن كان هو الواحد الموجود في الجزء الأول المنسحب إلى الآخر فهذا هو الجواب الأول، والإلزام تعدد الإبدال قطعاً، قلت: هب الواجب من الشرع صلاة واحدة لكن لا بوحدة متعينة بل أي وحدة كانت، (1) قوله : (حتى حكم الخ، كذا بالأصول التي عندنا ، وأصل العبارة في شرح محمد عبد الحق هكذا: «إن في الحج توسعة حتى حكم رسول الله الله بصحة حج صبي غير عاقل مع أمه فاكتفى الخ. والحديث في مسلم وغيره: وقعت امرأة صبياً لها فقال يا رسول الله ألهذا حج ؟ قال : نعم ولك أجر». اهـ، كتبه مصححه.
Issue: The time for performing the expanded obligation. (1) It is valid. When the obligation is expanded, all of the time is a time for its performance, so the responsible person is free to choose to perform it at any time he wishes within its estimated time, and he does not leave it throughout the entire time. Al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani and most Shafi'is said: The obligation at every moment is the act or the resolve as a substitute, and the act becomes specified at the end. They do not require (i.e., these scholars) renewal of resolve in every part, so that if he fails to have resolve in the second part, he disobeys. Rather, it is possible that their school is that the first resolve extends like the extension of intention until it becomes restricted. Then what is in al-Minhaj—that the substitute is multiple and the substituted is one—does not apply, and this does not exist in law. The reason for non-application is that we do not concede the multiplicity of substitutes, for it is not stated [in the texts]; so it may be one extended like the extension of intention. As for when two resolves exist, each is not a substitute in itself; rather, the substitute is one of them that exists within both, as in the characteristics of expiation. The specificity of the first and second has no role in the substitution. Moreover, the substituted is also multiple, for the occurrences of the act are according to the number of parts (i.e., the number of parts of time), and there is no doubt that those occurrences are obligatory as substitutes. For if he does not perform at the beginning of time, then the second occurrence becomes obligatory, and so on. Similarly, their resolves are multiple, so the occurrences equal the resolves as substitutes. If it is said: The obligation is only the prayer, and there is no multiplicity in it; rather, multiplicity is in the partial occurrences. So the substituted is one and the substitute is many. I say: The absolute resolve is one resolve substituting for the absolute prayer, and its particulars are like its particulars. If you say: The Law only obligated one prayer, not many prayers, but expanded; so at every part a substitute of one prayer is obligatory, and if the resolve-substitute is the one existing in the first part extending to the end, that is the first answer, and the multiplicity of substitutes is necessarily required. I say: Suppose the obligation from the Law is one prayer, but not by a specific unity; rather, any unity. (1) His statement: 'until he ruled...' as in our sources, and the original wording in the commentary of Muhammad Abd al-Haqq is: 'Indeed, in Hajj there is expansion until the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, ruled for the validity of the Hajj of an irrational boy with his mother, and he sufficed...' And the hadith in Muslim and others: A woman fell with her son and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, does he have Hajj?' He said: 'Yes, and you have a reward.' End. Recorded by its corrector.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling for an expanded obligation (واجب موسع) such as the five daily prayers, which have a defined time window. The author states that the entire time is valid for performance, and the responsible person may perform the act at any point. He then presents the view of al-Baqillani and the majority of Shafi'is, who hold that at every moment of the time, the obligation is either to perform the act or to have the resolve (عزم) to perform it as a substitute. They do not require renewing this resolve at each moment; the initial resolve suffices until the time becomes restricted. The author counters an objection from al-Minhaj that the substitute is multiple while the substituted is one, arguing that the resolve can be considered one continuous intention. He uses the example of expiation characteristics (خصال الكفارة) where multiple options exist but the substitute is one. Then he engages in a dialectical exchange: if the obligation is only one prayer, why would there be multiple substitutes? He responds that the absolute resolve is a substitute for the absolute prayer, and its extension covers the entire time. The footnote references the previous lesson's hadith about a boy's Hajj indicating expansion in acts of worship.

Key Terms
الواجب الموسع (al-wajib al-muwassa'): An obligation whose performance time is broader than needed for the act itself, e.g., the five daily prayers.
العزم (al-azm): Resolve: the inner determination to perform the obligation, considered a substitute for the actual act at each moment before performance.
البدل (al-badal): Substitute: the azm that stands in for the actual performance until it is done.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in this passage, what is required at each moment of an expanded obligation's time?
A) The actual performance of the act at every moment.
B) A renewed resolve (azm) in every part of the time.
C) Nothing beyond the initial intention; the entire time is valid for performance, and one may delay without sin until the end.
D) The resolve must be continuous and explicit at every moment.

Key Takeaway
In an expanded obligation, the entire time is valid; the obligation is to perform the act within the time, not to constantly intend.

Intention for Obligatory vs Supererogatory Acts
A ruling on intention specification for fard vs nafl acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule regarding absolute intention for fard and nafl acts, and explain the rational basis for why absolute intention suffices for fard but not nafl.

Core Idea
Absolute intention suffices for fard; intending nafl fails because supererogation contradicts obligation.

This passage tackles a critical usul question: when you begin a prayer, does your intention need to specify whether it is fard or nafl? The Hanafi school rules that if you intend absolutely—that is, without specifying—the act counts as obligatory if that was your underlying intent. But if you intend it as supererogatory, it cannot become obligatory because the two categories conflict. This reasoning is not just abstract; it affects every prayer you pray. By understanding the rationale, you will see how usul principles govern even the simplest acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on absolute intention
The passage states: 'His obligatory act is performed by absolute intention.' That means if you intend a prayer with a general, non-specific intention, and you are actually performing an obligatory prayer, it counts as fard. Find this statement in the Arabic.
The key phrase is 'يتأدى فرضه بمطلق النية'.
2
Understand why the reverse is invalid
The passage explains that if you intend it as nafl, it cannot become fard because 'supererogatoriness opposes obligatoriness.' The categories are contradictory; a single act cannot be both. Contrast this with absolute intention, which does not contradict fard.
The phrase 'النفلية تضاد الفرضية' expresses the contradiction.
3
Analyze the rational argument (dalil aqli)
The reasoning: if absolute intention worked for nafl but not fard, then no absolute intention would ever yield fard, which is false. Also, the obligatory act is immediate (fawri) but does not make the time sacred, so specification is needed—except for Ramadan, where the time itself specifies. Identify these points.
Focus on the logical structure: 'لو عكس لزم أن لا يقع فرض بمطلق النية'.
4
Examine the hadith example of Hajj
The passage cites a hadith about a child's Hajj: the mother's intention for her non-rational child sufficed. This shows that absolute intention works for Hajj, so it should work for other fard acts. Identify the lesson here.
The hadith is in Muslim: 'إن حج ابنك'.
5
Apply the usul principle to a scenario
Consider a person who enters a mosque intending to pray 'just a prayer' without specifying. If it is time for Zuhr, the prayer counts as Zuhr (fard). If they intended nafl, it becomes nafl but not fard. Walk through this using the passage's reasoning.
This tests understanding of the rule's application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فافهم وتأمل فإنه حقيق به ومن ها هنا أي من أجل شبهة بالمعيار والظرف أعطى حكماً بين حكميهما فقلنا : يتأدى فرضه بمطلق النية، ويقع عن النفل إذا نواه) وإنما لم يعكس، لأن النفلية تضاد الفرضية وليست مبطلة له كما في المعيار، والإطلاق لا يضادها، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أنه : هل يصلح العام الأول النفل أم لا؟ وعلى الثاني يلزم أن يصح بنية النفل أيضاً، وعلى الأول فلا يكفي الإطلاق، فإن المؤدى لم يتعين للفرض وأيضاً الواجب، وإن كان واجباً فورياً، لكن غايته حرمة غيره لا أنه صار الوقت في حق ما عداه كالمحرم، فلا بد من نية التعين بخلاف شهر رمضان والحق في وجهه أن في الحج توسعة حتى حكم رسول الله له لتلك كل المرأة إن حج ابنك وكان غير عاقل تام فاكتفى بنية أمه، فأولى أن بنية مطلقة من الحاج وأما النفلية فمضادة بالكلية فلا يصح بنيتها هذا والله أعلم بمراد عباده وهو علام الغيوب.
(1) قوله : (حتى حكم الخ، كذا بالأصول التي عندنا ، وأصل العبارة في شرح محمد عبد الحق هكذا: «إن في الحج توسعة حتى حكم رسول الله الله بصحة حج صبي غير عاقل مع أمه فاكتفى الخ. والحديث في مسلم وغيره: وقعت امرأة صبياً لها فقال يا رسول الله ألهذا حج ؟ قال : نعم ولك أجر». اهـ، كتبه مصححه.
So understand and reflect, for it is worthy of that. And from here, i.e., because of the ambiguity of the measuring standard and container, a ruling was given between their two rulings. We said: His obligatory act is performed by absolute intention, and it occurs as supererogatory if he intends it. And it is not reversed, because supererogatoriness opposes obligatoriness but does not invalidate it, as in the measuring standard, while absoluteness does not oppose it. And it is not hidden from you whether the first general intention suffices for supererogatory or not. On the latter, it would require that it be valid also by intending supererogatory, and on the former, absoluteness would not suffice, because what is performed is not specified as obligatory. Also the obligatory, though immediate, its ultimate consequence is prohibition of something else, not that the time becomes like a prohibition regarding others. So specification of intention is necessary, unlike the month of Ramadan. The truth in its aspect is that in Hajj there is extension, to the point that the Messenger of God ruled for that woman: 'If your son performs Hajj...' and he was not fully rational, so he sufficed with the mother's intention. So it is more fitting that an absolute intention from the pilgrim suffices. As for supererogatoriness, it is completely contradictory, so intention of it is not valid. This, and God knows best His servants' intentions, and He is the Knower of the unseen. (1) His statement: 'until he ruled...' etc., as in the manuscripts we have. The original expression in Sharh Muhammad Abd al-Haq is: 'Indeed in Hajj there is extension, to the point that the Messenger of God ruled for the validity of Hajj of a non-rational child with his mother, and sufficed with the mother's intention. The hadith is in Muslim and others: A woman presented her son and said: O Messenger of God, is there Hajj for this one? He said: Yes, and for you is reward.' End. Written by its corrector.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and its proof regarding the role of intention in distinguishing obligatory (fard) from supererogatory (nafl) acts in Hanafi fiqh. The author explains why absolute intention suffices for fard but not for nafl, and why the reverse is invalid. The key reasoning is that supererogatoriness contradicts obligatoriness in essence, but absoluteness does not. Therefore, if one intends a fard act with absolute intention (without specifying fard or nafl), the act counts as fard. But if one intends it as nafl, it does not become fard. The opposite—that absolute intention could work for nafl but not fard—is dismissed because then absolute intention would never produce fard, which is false. An analogy is drawn with Hajj: there is extension (tawse'ah) in Hajj, so absolute intention suffices for the pilgrim, as seen in the hadith about a child's Hajj where the mother's intention was sufficient. The footnote clarifies the hadith reference. This ruling is based on rational reasoning (dalil aqli) and the nature of worship categories.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention in the heart that distinguishes one act of worship from another
فرض (fard): An obligatory act that is definitively required in the religion
نفل (nafl): A supererogatory act, recommended but not obligatory

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling regarding an obligatory act performed with absolute intention?
A) It counts as supererogatory
B) It counts as obligatory
C) It is invalid
D) It requires the intention of fard explicitly

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, absolute intention suffices for obligatory acts because supererogation contradicts obligation, but absoluteness does not.

The Time of Obligation in Wajib Mawsu': Three Views and the Hanafi Position
Debate on time of wajib mawsu' and refutation of specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three views on the time of wajib mawsu' and explain why the Hanafi school holds the entire time as the time of obligation.

Core Idea
For wajib mawsu', the entire time is the time of obligation — the mukallaf has choice within it.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut presents a key usul dispute: when exactly is the wajib mawsu' obligatory? Some say only at the beginning, others only at the end, but the Hanafi school argues the entire time is the time of obligation. Understanding this distinction is crucial for identifying the correct ruling of an act performed at different times.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three views on the time of wajib mawsu'
List the three positions: (1) Some Shafi'is and theologians say the time is only the beginning, so delay is qada and sinful. (2) Some Iraqi Hanafis say only the end is the time, so early performance is nafl. (3) The mainstream Hanafi view (supported by al-Karkhi) holds the entire time is the time of obligation.
Be careful: the attribution of the end-time view to Hanafis is considered a mistake by the author.
2
State the Hanafi proof from consensus
The Hanafi proof is based on decisive consensus (ijma' qati'): the mukallaf is not considered sinful if he performs the act in any part of the time, before the emergence of these differing opinions. This consensus shows that the command is expansive, not restricted.
The phrase 'لأنه لو أتى في أي جزء لا يعد عاصياً بالإجماع القاطع' is the key evidence.
3
Understand al-Karkhi's conditional ruling
Al-Karkhi says: if the person remains under obligation (i.e., capable of performing) until the end of the time, then what he performed earlier is obligatory; otherwise (if he becomes incapacitated), it is nafl. This reconciles the expansive nature with the possibility of missing the deadline.
This shows that the obligation is tied to the entire time, not a fixed part.
4
Distinguish expansion from specification
Specifying the time to the beginning or end is a restriction (tadiq) that contradicts the expansion (tawsi'a) implied by the command. The command itself gave choice, so any narrowing requires evidence which is absent.
The author states: 'والتعيين بأول الوقت أو آخره تضييق مناف للتوسعة'.
5
Contrast practical consequences
Under the beginning-time view, delaying is sinful and requires qada. Under the end-time view, performing early is nafl that fulfills the obligation. Under the Hanafi view, any performance within the time is proper wajib, provided the person remains capable until the end.
The Hanafi view avoids the problem of defining 'early' or 'late' and preserves the unity of the obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقت المقالة الثانية في الأحكام فإن الواجب الصلاة في أي جزء وقعت ولا شك أن الصلاة الواقعة في الجزء الأول جزئي، وفي الجزء الثاني جزئي آخر ، فإذا لم يؤد في أول الجزء فيجب عليه الأداء في جزء آخر، بل إيقاعها في جزء آخر، وكذا الأعزام فتدبر إلا أن الواجب واحد موجود في هذه الجزئيات بالذات، والأعزام قد كثرت في الوجود فلا جواب إلا الأول (و) نقل (عن بعض الشافعية، وقيل : بل عن بعض المتكلمين وقته أوّله فإن أخره فقضاء) فينبغي على هذا أن يأثم بالتأخير أول الوقت (و) روي عن بعض الحنفية العراقيين ليس كل الوقت وقتاً للواجب (بل آخره) وقته (فإن قدمه فنفل يسقط به الفرض كالوضوء قبل الوقت، ونسب في المنهاج هذا القول إلى الحنفية، وهذه النسبة غلط، وما قال بعض شروحه أنهم قالوا ليس في أول الوقت واجب الأداء، ففيه أنه نفل لا محل له فإن نفس الوجوب لا يوجب نفلية المأتي به، بل ينافيها، ولو أتى به المكلف أتى بالواجب قطعاً (قال) الإمام أبو الحسن الكرخي (إن بقي) المؤدي في غير الآخر (بصفة التكليف إلى آخر الوقت فما قدمه واجب وإلا فنفل لنا أن الأمر وسع الفعل) وخير المكلف بالأداء في أي وقت شاء لأنه لو أتى في أي جزء لا يعد عاصياً بالإجماع القاطع قبل حدوث هذه الآراء. (والتعيين) بأول الوقت أو آخره (تضييق) مناف للتوسعة (والتخيير بين الفعل والعزم كما في قول القاضي (زيادة) على توسعة الآمر من غير دليل واستدل بأن المصلي في غير الآخر بل في «الوسط» (ممتثل) فليس الواجب في الأول والآخر إلا الامتثال ، ثم هو ممتثل لكونه مصلياً قطعاً لا لكونه آتياً بأحد الأمرين) فبطل قول القاضي (وربما تمنع المقدمة) المذكورة فإنها كيف يسلمها القاضي (فقيل إنها مجمع إجماعاً قطعياً فلا يصح المنع (أقول الإجماع على الامتثال بها بخصوصها في كل جزء فرع الإجماع على وجوبها فيه لأن الامتثال أداء الواجب كما وجب (وقد تقدم الخلاف فيه) فلا إجماع (فتأمل إشارة إلى منع الفرعية، مستنداً بأن الامتثال في وقت أعم من الوجوب فيه، والجواب أنا أردنا به إتيان المأمور به على وجهه، وهذا لا يحصل إلا بالإتيان كما ولك أن تقول في تقرير الدليل أن خروج المصلي في غير الآخر عن عهدة التكليف، إنما هو لإتيان الصلاة لا الإيمان) لا دخل فيه للوقت، ولا يصلح بدلاً عن الفعل، فإن المؤمن يجب عليه أن لا يريد الترك للواجب ألا ترى لو أخل بالعزم بأن أراد الترك عصى وإن لم يدخل الوقت فافهم، و) قال (في البديع :) لإبطال قول القاضي (لو كان العزم بدلاً عن الصلاة يسقط به المبدل كسائر الأبدال) وليس كذلك، فإن الصلاة لا تسقط حتى قال إنه يتعين آخراً (والجواب منع الملازمة، بل اللازم سقوط الوجوب وقد التزموه) فإنه يسقط الوجوب في ذلك الحين، وأما في الآخر فلا بدل، وفيه نظر ظاهر، فإنه إذا أتى بالبدل مرة سقط وجوب البدل ،والمبدل فتم امتثال الأمر، فإنه لا يقتضي التكرار، فإن وجب وجب بأمر آخر، فهذا واجب آخر ولا كلام فيه فتأمل، وهذا ما عندي؛ وأيضاً يلزم أن لا يكون المؤدى بعد العزم في وسط الوقت ممتثلاً لعدم بقاء الوجوب، والامتثال حقيقة ليس إلا أداء الواجب كما وجب اللهم إلا أن يلتزم ويقول : نفل يسقط به الفرض، وأيضاً: يلزم أن لا هذا المؤدى، لأنه إن أدى بنية الواجب فلا يصح واجب، وإن أدى بنية النفل أو مطلق النية فلم يذهب إليه أحد في الموسع فتأمل وأنصف فإنه دقيق. بعض الحنفية قالوا: لو كان واجباً أوّلاً عصى بتأخيره وفي الكشف بعبارة أخرى : الإيجاب في أول الوقت والتخيير فيه متنافيان، لأن الإيجاب يقتضي المنع عن الترك، والتخيير يجوزه (قلنا) اللزوم (ممنوع ، وإنما يلزم لو كان الوجوب (مضيقاً) بل إنما وجب موسعاً ولا تنافي، فإن الوجوب الموسع مانع عن الترك في كل الوقت والتخيير إنما هو في أجزاء الوقت بشرط أن لا يخل به في كل الوقت بعض الشافعية قالوا لو كان واجباً في الآخر لما صح في الأول، قلنا ،ممنوع وإنما لو كان فيه بخصوصه، بل هو موسع من الأول إلى الآخر.
Time of the second thesis on rulings: For the obligatory prayer, it falls in any part; and there is no doubt that the prayer occurring in the first part is one partial, and in the second part another partial. So if one does not perform it in the first part, then he must perform it in another part, rather its occurrence in another part. And similarly the resolves, so reflect, except that the obligatory is one, existing in these partials in essence, and the resolves have multiplied in existence, so there is no answer except the first. (And) it is transmitted (from some Shafi'is, and it was said rather from some theologians: its time is its beginning, so if he delays it, it is qada). So accordingly, he should sin by delaying in the first part of the time. (And) it is narrated from some Hanafis of Iraq: not all the time is time for the obligatory, (but its end) is its time, (so if he brings it forward, it is nafl that fulfills the obligation, like wudu before the time. And in al-Minhaj, this saying is attributed to the Hanafis, and this attribution is a mistake. And what some of its commentaries said that they said: there is no obligatory of performance in the first part of the time, so in it, it is a nafl with no place, for the very obligation does not obligate the nafl-ness of what is performed, rather it contradicts it. And if the obligated person performs it, he definitely performs the obligatory. (Al-Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi said): (if what is performed remains) in other than the end (under the quality of obligation until the end of the time, then what he offered is obligatory; otherwise, it is nafl. For us, the command made the act broad) and gave the mukallaf the choice to perform at any time he wishes, because if he performs in any part, he is not counted as disobedient by decisive consensus before the occurrence of these opinions. (And specification) to the beginning or end (is a restriction) contradictory to expansion. (And the choice between the act and the resolve as in the statement of al-Qadi (is an addition) to the expansion of the commander without evidence. And he argued that the prayer-performing person in other than the end, rather in the middle, (is compliant), so the obligatory in the first and last is nothing but compliance, then he is compliant because he is a prayer performer definitely, not because he is bringing one of the two matters. So al-Qadi's statement is invalidated. (And perhaps the mentioned premise is denied) for how would al-Qadi concede it? (So it was said that it is agreed upon by decisive consensus, so denial is not correct. (I say): consensus on compliance with it particularly in every part is branch of consensus on its obligation in it, because compliance is performance of the wajib as it is wajib. (And the disagreement on it has preceded), so there is no consensus. (So reflect) as an indication of denial of the branchhood, based on the fact that compliance in a time is more general than obligation in it. And the answer: we meant by it the bringing of the commanded act in its proper manner, and this is not attained except by bringing it as it is. And you may say in stating the proof: the exit of the prayer performer in other than the end from the responsibility of obligation is only due to bringing the prayer, not due to bringing one of the two matters, and consensus on this does not depend on consensus on the expanded obligation. Reflect. Waqif al-Asrar (may Allah sanctify his secret) said: exit from the responsibility of obligation is branch of its existence, and the responsibility is the obligation. Then if the speech were refined on the method of denial and what is mentioned were made support, this saying and counter-saying would be removed. Then I say: the opponent does not say with substitution from both sides, such that prayer is a substitute for resolve and resolve for prayer like the characteristics of expiation, but here prayer is (original) and resolve is (substitute). So compliance with prayer in particular, because it is original, does not harm it, just as compliance with the wudu of the excused person because it is original does not harm the obligation of tayammum as a substitute for it. So reflect, for it is subtle. Al-Qadi and his followers (said): if he brings one of them, it suffices him, and if he neglects both, he disobeys, so the wajib is one of them. We say: disobedience is denied on the assumption of neglecting both, for how? And often in the first part of the time the act or its will is not present. So it should be that if it is said: by resolve is meant not intending to leave, we say: it is accepted that it is wajib, but it is from the rulings of faith, not entering into the time, and it is not valid as a substitute for the act. For the believer must not intend to leave the wajib. Do you not see that if he neglects the resolve by intending to leave, he disobeys even if the time has not entered? So understand. And (he said) in al-Badi' (to invalidate al-Qadi's statement): if resolve were a substitute for prayer, the substitutee would be dropped by it like other substitutes, but it is not so, for prayer is not dropped until he said it becomes specific at the end. (And the answer is: denial of the implication, but the necessary is dropping of the obligation, and they committed to it). For the obligation drops at that moment, but at the end there is no substitute. And in it is apparent consideration: if he brings the substitute once, the obligation of the substitute and the substitutee drop, then the command has been complied with, for it does not require repetition. If it becomes obligatory, it is obligatory by another command, and this is another obligation and no speech about it. And also it would follow that what is performed after the resolve in the middle of the time is not a compliant because of the non-continuation of the obligation, and compliance in reality is nothing but performance of the wajib as it is wajib, unless he commits and says: nafl that fulfills the obligation. And also it would follow that this performed act is not valid, because if he performs with the intention of the wajib, it is not valid as wajib, and if he performs with the intention of nafl or absolute intention, no one has gone to that in the expanded act. So reflect and be just, for it is subtle. Some Hanafis said: if it were obligatory at the beginning, he would sin by delaying it. And in al-Kashf in another expression: obligation at the beginning of the time and choice in it are contradictory, because obligation necessitates prevention from leaving, and choice permits it. (We say): the necessity (is denied), and it would only be necessary if the obligation were (restricted), but rather it is obligated in an expanded manner and there is no contradiction. For the expanded obligation prevents from leaving in all the time, and choice is only in the parts of the time on condition that he does not neglect it in all the time. Some Shafi'is said: if it were obligatory at the end, it would not be valid at the beginning. We say: denied, and it would only be if it were specific to it, but rather it is expanded from the beginning to the end.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut is a detailed discussion on the nature of the expanded obligatory act (wajib mawsu'), specifically focusing on the time of obligation and whether the act of resolve (azm) can serve as a substitute. The author presents multiple views: some Shafi'is and theologians say the time is only the beginning, and delay necessitates qada. Some Iraqi Hanafis say only the end is the time. Imam al-Karkhi presents a nuanced view: if the person remains capable until the end, what he did earlier is obligatory; otherwise it is nafl. The Hanafi position is that the entire time is the time of obligation, and the mukallaf has the choice to perform at any part, as the command is expansive (musawwa'). The author then addresses the argument of al-Qadi who says that the act and resolve are two options and the wajib is one of them. The author refutes this by showing that resolve is not a valid substitute in the expanded duty because it is a ruling of faith not tied to the time, and acting on the original (prayer) suffices. The passage includes intricate dialectic and counter-arguments, emphasizing that the consensus on compliance does not require consensus on the expanded obligation. The author concludes that some later Hanafis also argued about the contradiction of obligation and choice, but the correct view is that obligation is expanded and consistent with choice within the time frame.

Key Terms
الواجب الموسع (al-wajib al-mawsu'): The obligatory act that is required to be performed within a specified time frame, but the specific time of performance within that frame is left to the choice of the mukallaf.
التوسعة (al-tawsi'a): The expansion of the command, meaning the obligation is spread over the entire time, not pinpointed to a particular moment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in the passage, what is the time of obligation for a wajib mawsu' (expanded obligatory act)?
A) Only the first part of the time
B) Only the last part of the time
C) The entire time from beginning to end
D) The middle part of the time

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the wajib mawsu' is owed over the entire time frame, giving the mukallaf choice; specification to a part is a restriction without evidence.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Refuting the Substitution of Resolve (Azm) for the Act in Expanded Obligations
Refutation of resolve as substitute in wajib mawsu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rejects the view that resolve (azm) can substitute for the actual act in a wajib mawsu' and identify the key arguments against it.

Core Idea
Resolve (azm) is a ruling of faith, not a substitute for the act in expanded obligations.

In the same passage, the author addresses a controversial view attributed to some scholars (al-Qadi) that in a wajib mawsu', the mukallaf has a choice between performing the act or having a firm resolve (azm) to perform it later. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi refutation, showing that resolve cannot substitute because it is a continuous obligation of faith unrelated to the time, and that allowing substitution would lead to logical contradictions.

Guided Path
1
State the view of al-Qadi and his followers
Al-Qadi held that the wajib in a mawsu' is one of two things: either the act or the resolve to perform it. If the mukallaf brings either, he is compliant; if he neglects both, he disobeys. This makes the wajib a choice (mukhayyar) between act and resolve.
This is similar to the concept of takhyir in kaffara, where one chooses among options.
2
Identify the Hanafi response
The Hanafis deny that disobedience occurs if both are neglected; often in the first part of time, the act or its will may not be present, yet one is not sinful. Moreover, resolve is a ruling of faith not tied to time—one must always intend not to leave the wajib, even before the time enters. Thus it cannot be a substitute for the act.
The author says: 'العزم من أحكام الإيمان لا دخل فيه للوقت'.
3
Refute the substitute logic
If resolve were a substitute, then bringing it should drop the obligation for the entire time, but the opponents themselves say that if one resolves early, the act becomes specific at the end (i.e., obligation remains). This shows resolve is not a true substitute. The author uses an analogy: in kaffara, a substitute fully replaces the original; here it does not.
The text says: 'لو كان العزم بدلاً عن الصلاة يسقط به المبدل كسائر الأبدال وليس كذلك'.
4
Analyze the consequence of accepting substitution
If resolve is accepted as a substitute at the beginning, then the obligation drops at that moment. Later, if one performs the act after the resolve, it is no longer wajib but nafl. But the opponents claim that after resolve, the act at the end is still wajib (or fulfilling). This contradiction shows the flaw.
Also, if obligation drops, the act performed later cannot be 'compliance' as the person is no longer obligated.
5
Conclude with the Hanafi position
The only valid view is that the wajib mawsu' is the act itself, and resolve is a separate continuous obligation. The act is original; resolve is not a substitute but a condition of faith.
The analogy with wudu of the excused person (who uses tayammum) shows that the original (wudu) is primary, and tayammum is substitute only when original is impossible.

وقت المقالة الثانية في الأحكام فإن الواجب الصلاة في أي جزء وقعت ولا شك أن الصلاة الواقعة في الجزء الأول جزئي، وفي الجزء الثاني جزئي آخر ، فإذا لم يؤد في أول الجزء فيجب عليه الأداء في جزء آخر، بل إيقاعها في جزء آخر، وكذا الأعزام فتدبر إلا أن الواجب واحد موجود في هذه الجزئيات بالذات، والأعزام قد كثرت في الوجود فلا جواب إلا الأول (و) نقل (عن بعض الشافعية، وقيل : بل عن بعض المتكلمين وقته أوّله فإن أخره فقضاء) فينبغي على هذا أن يأثم بالتأخير أول الوقت (و) روي عن بعض الحنفية العراقيين ليس كل الوقت وقتاً للواجب (بل آخره) وقته (فإن قدمه فنفل يسقط به الفرض كالوضوء قبل الوقت، ونسب في المنهاج هذا القول إلى الحنفية، وهذه النسبة غلط، وما قال بعض شروحه أنهم قالوا ليس في أول الوقت واجب الأداء، ففيه أنه نفل لا محل له فإن نفس الوجوب لا يوجب نفلية المأتي به، بل ينافيها، ولو أتى به المكلف أتى بالواجب قطعاً (قال) الإمام أبو الحسن الكرخي (إن بقي) المؤدي في غير الآخر (بصفة التكليف إلى آخر الوقت فما قدمه واجب وإلا فنفل لنا أن الأمر وسع الفعل) وخير المكلف بالأداء في أي وقت شاء لأنه لو أتى في أي جزء لا يعد عاصياً بالإجماع القاطع قبل حدوث هذه الآراء. المنع (أقول الإجماع على الامتثال بها بخصوصها في كل جزء فرع الإجماع على وجوبها فيه لأن الامتثال أداء الواجب كما وجب (وقد تقدم الخلاف فيه) فلا إجماع (فتأمل إشارة إلى منع الفرعية، مستنداً بأن الامتثال في وقت أعم من الوجوب فيه، والجواب أنا أردنا به إتيان المأمور به على وجهه، وهذا لا يحصل إلا بالإتيان كما ولك أن تقول في تقرير الدليل أن خروج المصلي في غير الآخر عن عهدة التكليف، إنما هو لإتيان الصلاة لا لإتيان أحد الأمرين والإجماع على هذا لا يتوقف على الإجماع على الوجوب الموسع تدبر، قال واقف الأسرار قدس سره الخروج عن عهدة التكليف فرع وجودها، والعهدة هي الوجوب، ثم لو حرر الكلام على طريقة المنع، وجعل المذكور سنداً لارتفع هذا القيل والقال من البين فتدبر (ثم أقول : الخصم لا يقول بالبدلية من الطرفين) بأن تكون الصلاة بدلاً من العزم والعزم من الصلاة كخصال الكفارة ، بل) ها هنا الصلاة (أصل و) العزم (خلف موسع من الأول إلى الآخر.
Time of the second thesis on rulings: For the obligatory prayer, it falls in any part; and there is no doubt that the prayer occurring in the first part is one partial, and in the second part another partial. Then if the speech were refined on the method of denial and what is mentioned were made support, this saying and counter-saying would be removed. Then I say: the opponent does not say with substitution from both sides, such that prayer is a substitute for resolve and resolve for prayer like the characteristics of expiation, but here prayer is (original) and resolve is (substitute). So compliance with prayer in particular, because it is original, does not harm it, just as compliance with the wudu of the excused person because it is original does not harm the obligation of tayammum as a substitute for it. So reflect, for it is subtle. Al-Qadi and his followers (said): if he brings one of them, it suffices him, and if he neglects both, he disobeys, so the wajib is one of them. We say: disobedience is denied on the assumption of neglecting both, for how? And often in the first part of the time the act or its will is not present. So it should be that if it is said: by resolve is meant not intending to leave, we say: it is accepted that it is wajib, but it is from the rulings of faith, not entering into the time, and it is not valid as a substitute for the act. For the believer must not intend to leave the wajib. Do you not see that if he neglects the resolve by intending to leave, he disobeys even if the time has not entered? So understand. And (he said) in al-Badi' (to invalidate al-Qadi's statement): if resolve were a substitute for prayer, the substitutee would be dropped by it like other substitutes, but it is not so, for prayer is not dropped until he said it becomes specific at the end. (And the answer is: denial of the implication, but the necessary is dropping of the obligation, and they committed to it). For the obligation drops at that moment, but at the end there is no substitute. And in it is apparent consideration: if he brings the substitute once, the obligation of the substitute and the substitutee drop, then the command has been complied with, for it does not require repetition. If it becomes obligatory, it is obligatory by another command, and this is another obligation and no speech about it. And also it would follow that what is performed after the resolve in the middle of the time is not a compliant because of the non-continuation of the obligation, and compliance in reality is nothing but performance of the wajib as it is wajib, unless he commits and says: nafl that fulfills the obligation. And also it would follow that this performed act is not valid, because if he performs with the intention of the wajib, it is not valid as wajib, and if he performs with the intention of nafl or absolute intention, no one has gone to that in the expanded act. So reflect and be just, for it is subtle. Some Hanafis said: if it were obligatory at the beginning, he would sin by delaying it. And in al-Kashf in another expression: obligation at the beginning of the time and choice in it are contradictory, because obligation necessitates prevention from leaving, and choice permits it. (We say): the necessity (is denied), and it would only be necessary if the obligation were (restricted), but rather it is obligated in an expanded manner and there is no contradiction. For the expanded obligation prevents from leaving in all the time, and choice is only in the parts of the time on condition that he does not neglect it in all the time. Some Shafi'is said: if it were obligatory at the end, it would not be valid at the beginning. We say: denied, and it would only be if it were specific to it, but rather it is expanded from the beginning to the end.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut is a detailed discussion on the nature of the expanded obligatory act (wajib mawsu'), specifically focusing on the time of obligation and whether the act of resolve (azm) can serve as a substitute. The author presents multiple views: some Shafi'is and theologians say the time is only the beginning, and delay necessitates qada. Some Iraqi Hanafis say only the end is the time. Imam al-Karkhi presents a nuanced view: if the person remains capable until the end, what he did earlier is obligatory; otherwise it is nafl. The Hanafi position is that the entire time is the time of obligation, and the mukallaf has the choice to perform at any part, as the command is expansive (musawwa'). The author then addresses the argument of al-Qadi who says that the act and resolve are two options and the wajib is one of them. The author refutes this by showing that resolve is not a valid substitute in the expanded duty because it is a ruling of faith not tied to the time, and acting on the original (prayer) suffices. The passage includes intricate dialectic and counter-arguments, emphasizing that the consensus on compliance does not require consensus on the expanded obligation. The author concludes that some later Hanafis also argued about the contradiction of obligation and choice, but the correct view is that obligation is expanded and consistent with choice within the time frame.

Key Terms
العزم (al-'azm): The firm resolve or intention to perform the obligatory act in the future, considered by some as a substitute for the actual act.
البدل (al-badal): Substitute; in usul, something that entirely replaces the original obligation (e.g., tayammum for wudu).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi refutation in the passage, why cannot resolve (azm) be a substitute for the act in a wajib mawsu'?
A) Because resolve is a ruling of faith not tied to the time
B) Because the time is too short
C) Because the act is more important
D) Because resolve is not mentioned in the Quran

Key Takeaway
Resolve (azm) is a continuous obligation of faith, not a substitute for the act in expanded duties; the wajib must be physically performed.

The Cause of the Expanded Wajib: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Debate on the cause of the expanded wajib between Hanafis and Shafi'is, with a proof from consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conflicting positions on the cause (sabab) of the expanded wajib (Hanafi vs. Shafi'i) and apply the Hanafi ijma-based proof to defend the expanded view.

Core Idea
The cause of an expanded wajib is not one moment; it transfers across the time, proven by consensus on obligation for latecomers.

This passage tackles a core usul question: what triggers an obligation that can be performed over a span of time? The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ on whether the cause (sabab) is the first part of the time specifically or the entire period. By examining the Hanafi proof from ijma, we see how the school derives a ruling that accommodates late-coming obligation.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the Shafi'i view (cause = first part of time specifically) and the Hanafi view (cause expanded across whole time, transferring from part to part).
The Shafi'i argument rests on precedence (al-sabq) and lack of competition.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof from ijma
The passage cites consensus (ijma) that a person who becomes Muslim or reaches puberty in the middle of the time is still obligated. If the cause were only the first part, such a person would have no obligation—contradicting ijma.
This is a proof by entailment: the fact of obligation proves the cause must be spread.
3
Understand the logical necessity
If the cause were fixed to the first part, a latecomer would have no cause for obligation. Since ijma says he is obligated, the cause must be capable of arising after the first part—hence it transfers.
The Hanafis further illustrate by imagining consecutive eligibilities in consecutive parts; no single part can be the exclusive cause.
4
Consider intra-Hanafi variations
Imam Zufar holds that the cause transfers to the part in which performance occurs (no causality after the performed part). Abu al-Yusr narrates that after time exits, the last part becomes the specific cause.
These are minority views within the Hanafi school; the established Hanafi position is that the cause continues to transfer until performance.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if someone becomes eligible mid-time, Shafi'is say no obligation (cause passed), Hanafis say obligation remains (cause transfers).
This directly affects whether prayers (e.g., Dhuhr) are required for new Muslims or those reaching puberty mid-time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة [سبب الواجب الموسع ]، السبب في الواجب الموسع الجزء الأول عيناً عند الشافعية للسبق) وعدم المزاحمة من الجزء الآخر وعند عامة (الحنفية ليس السبب الجزء الأول عيناً بل موسعاً إلى الأخير، كالمسبب فإنه موسع، وأراد بتوسيع السببية انتقالها يعني أن السبب الجزء الأول، إن اتصل الأداء حصل المقصود وتقرر السببية وإلا فالثاني وهكذا إلى الأخير (وعند) الإمام (زفر) الانتقال إلى ما الأداء وبعده لا سببية، فمن صار أهلاً في الجزء الذي لا يسعه لا تجب يسع الصلاة عليه عنده وعندنا تجب، وسيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى (وبعد الخروج) أي بعد خروج الوقت ولم يؤد (فالكل) سبب وروي عن أبي اليسر أن الجزء الأخير) من الوقت (متعين حينئذ أي حين الخروج للسببية (واستدل) أولاً (بالإجماع على الوجوب على من أسلم أو بلغ في وسط الوقت) وبالجملة صار أهلاً فيه ولو كان السبب الجزء الأول عيناً لما وجب عليه وإلا لزم الثبوت من غير سبب، وإن شئت فافرض الأهليات متعاقبة في أجزاء متعاقبة إلى الأخير، فلا يتعين جزء عيناً للسببية (ويمكن أن يجاب و يقال إنه أي الجزء المدرك (الأول في حقهما فتدبر) وهذا لا يصلح من قبل الشافعية وإنما هو إحداث احتمال آخر، والقول بأن السبب الجزء الأول المقارن للأهلية واستدل ثانياً بأن السبب إما الكل فيلزم أن لا تصح
Issue: [The cause of the expanded obligatory act] The cause in the expanded wajib is the first part specifically according to the Shafi'is, due to precedence and absence of competition from the other part. And according to the general (Hanafis), the cause is not the first part specifically, but is expanded to the last, like the effect for it is expanded. And he intended by expansion of causality its transmission, meaning that the cause is the first part: if the performance is connected, the purpose is achieved and the causality is established; otherwise, the second, and so on until the last. (And according to) Imam Zufar: transmission to what has performance and after it there is no causality. So one who becomes eligible in a part that he cannot accommodate the prayer is not obligated according to him, while according to us it is obligatory. And it will come, Allah willing. (And after the exit) i.e., after the time exits and he has not performed, (then all) are cause. And it is narrated from Abu al-Yusr that the last part of the time is then specific, i.e., at the time of exit, for causality. (And he argued) firstly (by consensus on the obligation on the one who becomes Muslim or reaches puberty in the middle of the time), and in general he becomes eligible in it. And if the cause were the first part specifically, it would not be obligatory upon him, otherwise establishment without cause would be necessary. And if you wish, assume the eligibilities consecutive in consecutive parts until the last, so no part is specifically determined for causality. (And it can be answered and said that it, i.e., the part that is realized, is the first in their right, so reflect). And this is not valid from the side of the Shafi'is, but is rather an innovation of another probability. And the saying that the cause is the first part concurrent with eligibility. And he argued secondly that the cause is either the whole, leading to its not being valid...
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage addresses the specific issue of the cause (sabab) of the expanded obligatory act (wajib mawsu'). It contrasts the Shafi'i position, which holds that the cause is specifically the first part of the time, with the Hanafi position, which maintains that the cause is expanded across the entire time, transferring from one part to the next if performance is delayed. Imam Zufar holds a different view: the cause transfers to the part in which performance occurs, and no causality remains thereafter. Abu al-Yusr narrates that after time exits, the last part becomes the specific cause. The author then provides a proof for the Hanafi position: the consensus that if someone becomes Muslim or reaches puberty in the middle of the time, the obligation is still upon him, which would not be the case if the cause were only the first part. Additionally, if you consider consecutive eligibility across different parts, no single part can be exclusively the cause. A possible Shafi'i response is mentioned but deemed invalid. The passage ends with a second proof that if the cause were the whole time, then it would lead to a problem, but the text cuts off.

Key Terms
السبب (al-sabab): The cause that triggers the obligation. In the context of the expanded wajib, it is the factor making the act obligatory.
السببية (al-sababyyah): The quality of being a cause; the causal relationship between the time and the obligation.
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of the scholars; used here as a proof for the Hanafi view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The first part of the time only
B) The last part of the time only
C) The entire time, transferring from part to part until performance
D) The middle part of the time only

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position on the expanded wajib is that its cause is transferred across the entire time, supported by the consensus that latecomers are still obligated.

The Cause of an Expanded Obligatory Act: Transfer of Causality
Dispute over which part of time is the cause for an expanded wajib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi doctrine of intiqal al-sababiyya to determine when an expanded wajib becomes obligatory and distinguish it from the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
The cause of an expanded wajib transfers from part to part; it is not fixed to the first part.

The five daily prayers have a broad time window. But which part of that window actually triggers the obligation? The Shafi'i school says the first part; the Hanafi majority says the cause transfers if you delay. This lesson unpacks the proof and the practical consequences of this difference.

Guided Path
1
Define the key terms
Understand sabab (cause) and wajib mawsu' (expanded obligatory act). The cause is that which the Lawgiver makes a sign for the ruling. An expanded wajib has a time window for performance.
The Hanafi definition of sabab is broader than the Shafi'i.
2
State the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'is hold that the cause is specifically the first part of the time due to precedence and lack of competition from other parts.
This leads to the view that the obligation is tied to the first part; delay may make the performance qada'.
3
State the Hanafi majority position
The cause is not a specific part but transfers from the first to the last. If you perform in the first part, causality is fixed there; if not, it moves to the second, and so on.
This is called intiqal al-sababiyya. Imam Zufar holds a variant: causality only transfers to the part in which actual performance occurs.
4
Examine the consensus proof
If a person embraces Islam or reaches puberty in the middle of the time, the prayer is unanimously obligatory. If the cause were only the first part, that part has passed, so the obligation would lack a cause. Thus the cause must be the part they become capable in.
This is the primary Hanafi proof. The text also presents a logical dilemma to refute the Shafi'i view.
5
Analyze the logical dilemma
If the cause were the whole time, prayer would only be valid after time ends. If the first part specifically, performance in the middle would be qada'. If the last part, performance before it invalid. So the only consistent view is transfer.
The Shafi'i can respond by choosing the second horn but claim causality is for an expanded obligation, so performance in any part is ada'.
6
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
For a person who becomes capable mid-time: Hanafi says obligation is immediate; Shafi'i says from the beginning (but may not have been obligated yet). Also, performing in the last part: Hanafi says valid as ada' with deficiency; Shafi'i may consider it qada'.
The text also discusses the branch: Asr prayer in the sunset redness is valid because causality transferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة [سبب الواجب الموسع ]
السبب في الواجب الموسع الجزء الأول عيناً عند الشافعية للسبق) وعدم المزاحمة من الجزء الآخر وعند عامة (الحنفية ليس السبب الجزء الأول عيناً بل موسعاً إلى الأخير، كالمسبب فإنه موسع، وأراد بتوسيع السببية انتقالها يعني أن السبب الجزء الأول، إن اتصل الأداء حصل المقصود وتقرر السببية وإلا فالثاني وهكذا إلى الأخير (وعند) الإمام (زفر) الانتقال إلى ما الأداء وبعده لا سببية، فمن صار أهلاً في الجزء الذي لا يسعه لا تجب يسع الصلاة عليه عنده وعندنا تجب، وسيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى (وبعد الخروج) أي بعد خروج الوقت ولم يؤد (فالكل) سبب وروي عن أبي اليسر أن الجزء الأخير) من الوقت (متعين حينئذ أي حين الخروج للسببية (واستدل) أولاً (بالإجماع على الوجوب على من أسلم أو بلغ في وسط الوقت) وبالجملة صار أهلاً فيه ولو كان السبب الجزء الأول عيناً لما وجب عليه وإلا لزم الثبوت من غير سبب، وإن شئت فافرض الأهليات متعاقبة في أجزاء متعاقبة إلى الأخير، فلا يتعين جزء عيناً للسببية (ويمكن أن يجاب و يقال إنه أي الجزء المدرك (الأول في حقهما فتدبر) وهذا لا يصلح من قبل الشافعية وإنما هو إحداث احتمال آخر، والقول بأن السبب الجزء الأول المقارن للأهلية واستدل ثانياً بأن السبب إما الكل فيلزم أن لا تصح الصلاة إلا بعد انقضاء الوقت، وأما الأول بعينه فيلزم أن يكون المؤدى في الوسط قضاء، وأما جزء أخير بعينه فيلزم أن لا يصح الأداء قبله : فتعين أن يكون كل سبباً على جهة الانتقال وفيه نظر لأن للخصم أن يختار الثاني ويقول : سببيته ليس للوجوب المضيق حتى يلزم كون المؤدى في الوسط قضاء بل السببية للوجوب الموسع ، فهو مفض إلى شغل ذمة المكلف بالأداء في أي جزء من أجزاء الوقت بعينه، ولا يؤخر عنه، كما في (خصال الكفارة)، الواجب أحد الأشياء مخيراً، وشيد الشيخ ابن الهمام أركان سببية الأول عيناً بأن انتقال السببية يكون أداء المسبب معرفاً للسببية، وهو قلب لموضوع السببية، لأنه تتقرر السببية على هذا الرأي على الجزء المقارن للأداء، فالجزء المقارن لا يعرف إلا بالأداء، وهذا ليس بشيء، لأن السبب عندنا الجزء الأول، وبه يثبت الواجب في الذمة، فإن أدى فبها وإلا انقضى هذا الجزء وتحقق آخر، فهو مفض إلى ثبوت الواجب ،وهكذا، وليس فيه كون الجزء المقارن بما هو مقارن سبباً حتى يلزم ما ذكر، قال واقف الأسرار أبي قدس سره : الوجوب الذي حدث من الجزء الأول هل بقي أم ارتفع ؟ على الأول : يلزم بسببية الجزء الثاني : إما تحصيل الحاصل أو وجوبان، وهما باطلان والثاني تصادمه الضرورة الوجدانية، ولا أقل من أنه قول نظري من غير حجة. وأيضاً : السببية ليست باعتبار منا، بل هي أمر اعتبره الشارع، فإذا كان الجزء الأول سبباً باعتبار الشارع، فإذا أدركه الأهل وجب المسبب، فلا يرتفع لعدم الأداء فلا انتقال كيف ولم يخرج المكلف عن عهدة التكليف الذي أفضى إليه السبب فالسبب في السببية كما كان، وتحقيق المقام أن الوقت كل جزء منه صالح للسببية، كما يظهر فيما إذا فرضت الأهليات متعاقبة فتعين البعض دون البعض تحكم، فالسبب للوجوب جزء ما من أجزاء هذا الوقت، ثم الوجوب موسع، ففي كل جزء منه يصح أداء الواجب والفعل الموجود في جزء غير الموجود في جزء آخر ضرورة أن الصلاة حركات وسكنات والزمان من مشخصاتها، ففي الجزء الأول كانت الحقيقة الصلاتية مطلوبة فيه، فإن أدى فيها وإلا صارت في الجزء الثاني مطلوبة، وهكذا، فالسبب الجزء الأول، لا لنفسه بل لكونه جزءاً ما، فإن أدى فيه تقرر السببية عليه وتفرغ الذمة، وإلا فوجد الجزء الثاني فهو السبب لا لأنه هو بخصوصه، بل لأنه جزء ما من أجزاء هذا الوقت، لكن اشتغل ذمة المكلف بالأداء في جزء آخر في شخص آخر، وهكذا وهذا هو المعنى بانتقال السببية، ومغايرة الإيقاعات بهذا الوجه كافية والاستدلال الثاني الذي عليه مدار الأئمة لا يفيد إلا سببية جزء ما لا ،بعينه وإذا خرج الوقت ولم يؤد نسب إلى كل الوقت، لا لأنه كل، كيف ولم يكن له دخل في الأداء فأنى يكون له دخل في القضاء بل لاشتماله على السبب الذي هو جزء ما هكذا ينبغي أن يفهم هذا المقام والتكلان على المفضل المنعام.
فرع
(صح عصر يومه في الجزء (الناقص) وهو وقت احمرار الشمس، لأن السببية، قد انتقلت إليه، فنقصانه أوجب ناقصاً وأدى كما وجب (لا) عصر (أمسه) أي لا يصح قضاء
Issue: [The cause of the expanded obligatory act]. The cause for the expanded obligatory act is specifically the first part according to the Shafi'is due to precedence and lack of competition from the other part. According to the majority of Hanafis, the cause is not specifically the first part but is expanded to the last, like the caused (obligation) is expanded. They intended by expanding the causality its transfer, meaning that the cause is the first part; if performance (act) is connected, the purpose is achieved and causality is established; otherwise the second, and so on until the last. According to Imam Zufar, causality transfers to what performance occurs in, and there is no causality after that. So someone who becomes legally capable in a part that does not accommodate the prayer, the prayer is not obligatory upon him according to him, but according to us it is obligatory. It will come, God willing. After exit (i.e., after the time has passed and he did not perform), then it is all a cause. And it is narrated from Abu al-Yusr that the last part of the time is specified then, i.e., at exit, for causality. He argued first by consensus on obligation upon one who embraces Islam or reaches puberty in the middle of time; in short, he becomes legally capable in it. If the cause were specifically the first part, it would not be obligatory upon him, otherwise it would necessitate establishment without a cause. And if you wish, suppose legal capacities occur successively in successive parts up to the last, then no part is specifically determined for causality. It can be answered and said that it (i.e., the part realized) is the first in their regard, so reflect. But this is not valid from the Shafi'i side; rather it is engendering another probability. And the statement that the cause is the first part concurrent with legal capacity. He argued secondly that if the cause is the whole, then it would necessitate that prayer is not valid except after the time ends. If it is specifically the first part, then that which is performed in the middle would be a make-up. If it is specifically a last part, then it would necessitate that performance before it is not valid. So it is determined that every part is a cause on the basis of transfer. But there is objection because the opponent can choose the second and say: its causality is not for the restricted obligation such that the performance in the middle would be a make-up; rather the causality is for the expanded obligation, so it leads to occupying the obligation's liability with performance in any specific part of the time, and not delaying it, as in the expiation options (khisal al-kafaarah), where the obligatory is one of the things by choice. And Shaykh Ibn al-Humam strengthened the pillars of the causality of the first part specifically by saying that the transfer of causality means performance of the caused defines the causality, and this inverts the subject of causality because according to this view causality is established on the part concurrent with performance, but the concurrent part is not known except by performance. This is nothing, because according to us the cause is the first part, and by it the obligation is established in the liability; if he performs, it is discharged; otherwise this part elapses and another is realized, so it leads to the establishment of the obligation, and so on. There is no making the concurrent part as concurrent a cause such that the mentioned consequence follows. The author of Asrar al-Asrar (may Allah sanctify his secret) said: Did the obligation arising from the first part remain or cease? On the first: the causality of the second part would necessitate either obtaining what is already obtained or two obligations, both invalid. On the second: it contradicts found necessary experience, and at the least it is a theoretical statement without proof. Also, causality is not by our consideration; rather it is a matter considered by the Lawgiver. So if the first part is a cause by the Lawgiver's consideration, then if the legally capable person reaches it, the caused becomes obligatory; it does not cease due to non-performance, so there is no transfer. How could it? The legally responsible person has not exited from the obligation that the cause led to, so the cause remains as it was. The investigation of the position is that every part of the time is suitable for causality, as appears when legal capacities are assumed successive; specifying some without others is arbitrary. So the cause for obligation is some part of the parts of this time. Then the obligation is expanded, so in every part it is valid to perform the obligatory act. The act found in one part is different from that found in another part necessarily because prayer is movements and pauses, and time is among its identifiers. So in the first part, the reality of prayer was demanded therein; if he performs therein, otherwise it becomes demanded in the second part, and so on. So the cause is the first part, not for itself but for being some part. If he performs in it, causality is established on it and the liability is discharged; otherwise the second part exists, so it is the cause, not because it is specifically it but because it is some part of the parts of this time. But the liability of the legally responsible becomes occupied with performance in another part in another person, and so on. This is the meaning of transfer of causality. The difference of the performances in this respect is sufficient. And the second argument, which is the basis of the imams, does not indicate except causality of some part, not specifically. And when time exits and he has not performed, it is attributed to the whole time, not because it is the whole (how can it be? It had no role in performance, so how can it have a role in make-up?) but because it encompasses the cause which is some part. This is how this position should be understood. And reliance is on the Bountiful Bestower.
Branch: The Asr prayer of the same day is valid in the deficient part, which is the time of sunset redness, because causality has transferred to it, so its deficiency obliges a deficient act, and it is performed as obligatory. The Asr prayer of the previous day is not valid as a make-up.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This is a detailed usul dispute regarding the cause (sabab) of an expanded obligatory act (wajib mawsu'), such as the five daily prayers that have a broad time window. The central question is: which part of the time is the cause that triggers the obligation? The Shafi'i position holds that the cause is specifically the first part of the time. The Hanafi majority holds that the cause is not a specific part but transfers from one part to the next; any part can become the cause if the act is performed or if the time passes. Imam Zufar, a Hanafi scholar, holds that causality transfers only to the part in which actual performance occurs, and after that there is no causality. The text first presents the consensus (ijma) argument: if a person becomes legally capable mid-time (e.g., converts to Islam or reaches puberty), the prayer is immediately obligatory. If the cause were only the first part, that part has already passed, so the obligation would have no cause. This proves the cause is not fixed to the first part. The Hanafi answer to this is that the first part in their regard (the part they become capable in) is considered the first for them. The second argument uses a dilemma: if the cause were the whole time, prayer would only be valid after time ends; if specifically the first part, performance in the middle would be a make-up; if the last part, performance before it would be invalid; therefore it must be a cause that transfers. However, the Shafi'i can respond by choosing the second horn but claiming the cause is for an expanded obligation, so performance in any part is valid. The text then discusses the refinement by Ibn al-Humam and others, concluding that every part is suitable for causality, and the transfer is not of the cause itself but of the locus of obligation. The branch (far') at the end applies this: performing Asr prayer in the deferred time (sunset redness) is valid because causality has transferred to that part, so the prayer is performed as obligatory, albeit deficient due to the time deficiency. However, performing the previous day's Asr qada' at that time is not valid because the time for performance has passed and the cause is no longer active.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): That which the Lawgiver (Shar'i) has made a sign for the existence of a legal ruling; in this context, the part of time that triggers the obligation of an expanded wajib.
واجب موسع (wajib mawsu'): An obligatory act with a broad time frame, e.g., the five daily prayers; the obligation is binding but can be performed at any time within the window.
انتقال السببية (intiqal al-sababiyya): The transfer of causality from one part of time to the next; the cause is not fixed but moves forward if the act is not performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi majority, what happens to the cause (sabab) for an expanded wajib if a person delays performance from the first part of time?
A) The cause remains on the first part, and the person is sinful for delaying.
B) The cause transfers to the second part, and so on until the last part.
C) The cause becomes invalid, and the obligation drops.
D) The cause moves to the last part only, making earlier performance invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the cause of an expanded wajib transfers from part to part, so performance in any part within the time is ada' (timely), and obligation arises immediately for those who become capable mid-time.
